# Prisma Client API

Complete API reference for Prisma Client queries and operations
The Prisma Client API reference documentation is based on the following schema:

```
model User { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) name String? email String @unique profileViews Int @default(0) role Role @default(USER) coinflips Boolean[] posts Post[] city String country String profile ExtendedProfile? pets Json } model ExtendedProfile { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) userId Int? @unique bio String? User User? @relation(fields: [userId], references: [id]) } model Post { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) title String published Boolean @default(true) author User @relation(fields: [authorId], references: [id]) authorId Int comments Json views Int @default(0) likes Int @default(0) } enum Role { USER ADMIN }
```


```
model User { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) name String? email String @unique profileViews Int @default(0) role Role @default(USER) coinflips Boolean[] posts Post[] city String country String profile ExtendedProfile? pets Json } model ExtendedProfile { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) userId Int? @unique bio String? User User? @relation(fields: [userId], references: [id]) } model Post { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) title String published Boolean @default(true) author User @relation(fields: [authorId], references: [id]) authorId Int comments Json views Int @default(0) likes Int @default(0) } enum Role { USER ADMIN }
```

All example generated types (such as UserSelect and UserWhereUniqueInput) are based on the User model.

```
UserSelect
```


```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```


```
User
```

## [PrismaClient](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#prismaclient)

[PrismaClient](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#prismaclient)

```
PrismaClient
```

This section describes the PrismaClient constructor and its parameters.

```
PrismaClient
```

### [adapter](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#adapter)
[adapter](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#adapter)

```
adapter
```

Specifies a [driver adapter](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/core-concepts/supported-databases/database-drivers#driver-adapters) for database connections. Required unless using [accelerateUrl](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#accelerateurl).

```
accelerateUrl
```


#### [Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example)
[Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example)

```
import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter });
```


```
import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter });
```

### [accelerateUrl](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#accelerateurl)
[accelerateUrl](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#accelerateurl)

```
accelerateUrl
```

Specifies a [Prisma Accelerate](https://www.prisma.io/accelerate) URL for remote query execution. Required unless using [adapter](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#adapter).

```
adapter
```


#### [Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-1)
[Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-1)

```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ accelerateUrl: process.env.ACCELERATE_URL, });
```


```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ accelerateUrl: process.env.ACCELERATE_URL, });
```

##### [Event types](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#event-types)
[Event types](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#event-types)
The query event type:

```
query
```


```
export type QueryEvent = { timestamp: Date; query: string; // Query sent to the database params: string; // Query parameters duration: number; // Time elapsed (in milliseconds) between client issuing query and database responding - not only time taken to run query target: string; };
```


```
export type QueryEvent = { timestamp: Date; query: string; // Query sent to the database params: string; // Query parameters duration: number; // Time elapsed (in milliseconds) between client issuing query and database responding - not only time taken to run query target: string; };
```

Note that for MongoDB, the params and duration fields will be undefined.

```
params
```


```
duration
```

All other log level event types:

```
export type LogEvent = { timestamp: Date; message: string; target: string; };
```


```
export type LogEvent = { timestamp: Date; message: string; target: string; };
```

### [log](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#log)

```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ log: [{ level: "query", emit: "event" }], }); prisma.$on("query", (e) => { console.log(e); }); async function main() { const countUsers = await prisma.user.count({}); } main() .then(async () => { await prisma.$disconnect(); }) .catch(async (e) => { console.error(e); await prisma.$disconnect(); process.exit(1); });
```


```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ log: [{ level: "query", emit: "event" }], }); prisma.$on("query", (e) => { console.log(e); }); async function main() { const countUsers = await prisma.user.count({}); } main() .then(async () => { await prisma.$disconnect(); }) .catch(async (e) => { console.error(e); await prisma.$disconnect(); process.exit(1); });
```

```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ log: [ { level: "warn", emit: "event" }, { level: "info", emit: "event" }, { level: "error", emit: "event" }, ], }); prisma.$on("warn", (e) => { console.log(e); }); prisma.$on("info", (e) => { console.log(e); }); prisma.$on("error", (e) => { console.log(e); }); async function main() { const countUsers = await prisma.user.count({}); } main() .then(async () => { await prisma.$disconnect(); }) .catch(async (e) => { console.error(e); await prisma.$disconnect(); process.exit(1); });
```

### [comments](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#comments)

[comments](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#comments)

```
comments
```

Defines an array of [SQL commenter plugins](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/observability-and-logging/sql-comments) that add metadata to your SQL queries as comments. This is useful for observability, debugging, and correlating queries with application traces.

#### [Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-1)
[Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-1)

```
SqlCommenterPlugin[]
```


#### [First-party plugins](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#first-party-plugins)
[First-party plugins](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#first-party-plugins)

```
@prisma/sqlcommenter-query-tags
```


```
AsyncLocalStorage
```


```
@prisma/sqlcommenter-trace-context
```


```
traceparent
```


#### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-2)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-2)

##### [Using first-party plugins](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#using-first-party-plugins)
[Using first-party plugins](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#using-first-party-plugins)

```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import { queryTags } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter-query-tags"; import { traceContext } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter-trace-context"; const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter, comments: [queryTags(), traceContext()], });
```


```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import { queryTags } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter-query-tags"; import { traceContext } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter-trace-context"; const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter, comments: [queryTags(), traceContext()], });
```


##### [Creating a custom plugin](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#creating-a-custom-plugin)
[Creating a custom plugin](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#creating-a-custom-plugin)

```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import type { SqlCommenterPlugin } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter"; const appPlugin: SqlCommenterPlugin = (context) => ({ application: "my-app", environment: process.env.NODE_ENV ?? "development", model: context.query.modelName, action: context.query.action, }); const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter, comments: [appPlugin], });
```


```
import { PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; import { PrismaPg } from "@prisma/adapter-pg"; import type { SqlCommenterPlugin } from "@prisma/sqlcommenter"; const appPlugin: SqlCommenterPlugin = (context) => ({ application: "my-app", environment: process.env.NODE_ENV ?? "development", model: context.query.modelName, action: context.query.action, }); const adapter = new PrismaPg({ connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL }); const prisma = new PrismaClient({ adapter, comments: [appPlugin], });
```

This produces SQL queries with comments like:

```
SELECT "id", "name" FROM "User" /*action='findMany',application='my-app',environment='production',model='User'*/
```


```
SELECT "id", "name" FROM "User" /*action='findMany',application='my-app',environment='production',model='User'*/
```

For more details, see [SQL comments](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/observability-and-logging/sql-comments).

### [transactionOptions](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#transactionoptions)

[transactionOptions](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#transactionoptions)

```
transactionOptions
```

Sets default [transaction options](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#transaction-isolation-level) globally.

#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks)
- The transaction levels can be overridden on a per-transaction level.

#### [Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-2)
[Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-2)

```
maxWait
```


```
timeout
```


```
isolationLevel
```

[transaction isolation level](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#transaction-isolation-level)

#### [Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-2)
[Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-2)

```
const prisma = new PrismaClient({ transactionOptions: { isolationLevel: Prisma.TransactionIsolationLevel.Serializable, maxWait: 5000, // default: 2000 timeout: 10000, // default: 5000 }, });
```


```
const prisma = new PrismaClient({ transactionOptions: { isolationLevel: Prisma.TransactionIsolationLevel.Serializable, maxWait: 5000, // default: 2000 timeout: 10000, // default: 5000 }, });
```

## [Model queries](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#model-queries)

[Model queries](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#model-queries)
Use model queries to perform [CRUD](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/crud) operations on your models. See also: CRUD

### [findUnique()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findunique)

[findUnique()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findunique)

```
findUnique()
```

findUnique() query lets you retrieve a single database record:

```
findUnique()
```

- By ID
- By a unique attribute

#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-1)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-1)
- Prisma Client's dataloader [automatically batches findUnique() queries](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/advanced/query-optimization-performance#using-findunique-with-the-fluent-api) with the same select and where parameters.
- If you want the query to throw an error if the record is not found, then consider using [findUniqueOrThrow](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow) instead.
- You cannot use [filter conditions](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#filter-conditions-and-operators) (e.g. equals, contains, not) to filter fields of the [JSON](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/reference/prisma-schema-reference#json) data type. Using filter conditions will likely result in a null response for that field.
[automatically batches findUnique() queries](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/advanced/query-optimization-performance#using-findunique-with-the-fluent-api)

```
findUnique()
```


```
select
```


```
where
```

[findUniqueOrThrow](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow)

```
findUniqueOrThrow
```

```

```



### [findUniqueOrThrow()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow)
[findUniqueOrThrow()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow)

```
findUniqueOrThrow()
```

findUniqueOrThrow() retrieves a single record in the same way as [findUnique()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findunique). However, if the query does not find the requested record, it throws a PrismaClientKnownRequestError.

```
findUniqueOrThrow()
```


```
findUnique()
```


```
PrismaClientKnownRequestError
```

Here's an example of its usage:

```
await prisma.user.findUniqueOrThrow({ where: { id: 1 }, });
```


```
await prisma.user.findUniqueOrThrow({ where: { id: 1 }, });
```

findUniqueOrThrow() differs from findUnique() as follows:

```
findUniqueOrThrow()
```


```
findUnique()
```

- 
Its return type is non-nullable. For example, post.findUnique() can return post or null, but post.findUniqueOrThrow() always returns post.

- 
It is not compatible with sequential operations in the [$transaction API](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#the-transaction-api). If the query throws a PrismaClientKnownRequestError, then the API will not roll back any operations in the array of calls. As a workaround, you can use interactive transactions with the $transaction API, as follows:
 $transaction(async (prisma) => {
   await prisma.model.create({ data: { ... });
   await prisma.model.findUniqueOrThrow();
 })

Its return type is non-nullable. For example, post.findUnique() can return post or null, but post.findUniqueOrThrow() always returns post.

```
post.findUnique()
```


```
post
```


```
null
```


```
post.findUniqueOrThrow()
```


```
post
```

It is not compatible with sequential operations in the [$transaction API](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#the-transaction-api). If the query throws a PrismaClientKnownRequestError, then the API will not roll back any operations in the array of calls. As a workaround, you can use interactive transactions with the $transaction API, as follows:

```
$transaction
```


```
PrismaClientKnownRequestError
```

```


```

### [findFirstOrThrow()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findfirstorthrow)
[findFirstOrThrow()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findfirstorthrow)

```
findFirstOrThrow()
```

findFirstOrThrow() retrieves a single data record in the same way as [findFirst()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findfirst). However, if the query does not find a record, it throws a PrismaClientKnownRequestError.

```
findFirstOrThrow()
```


```
findFirst()
```


```
PrismaClientKnownRequestError
```

findFirstOrThrow() differs from findFirst() as follows:

```
findFirstOrThrow()
```


```
findFirst()
```

- 
Its return type is non-nullable. For example, post.findFirst() can return post or null, but post.findFirstOrThrow always returns post.

- 
It is not compatible with sequential operations in the [$transaction API](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#the-transaction-api). If the query returns PrismaClientKnownRequestError, then the API will not roll back any operations in the array of calls. As a workaround, you can use interactive transactions with the $transaction API, as follows:
prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => {
  await tx.model.create({ data: { ... });
  await tx.model.findFirstOrThrow();
})

Its return type is non-nullable. For example, post.findFirst() can return post or null, but post.findFirstOrThrow always returns post.


##### [Create multiple new records](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#create-multiple-new-records)
[Create multiple new records](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#create-multiple-new-records)
In most cases, you can carry out batch inserts with the [createMany()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#createmany) or [createManyAndReturn()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#createmanyandreturn) queries. However, [there are scenarios where create() is the best option to insert multiple records](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-11).

```
createMany()
```


```
createManyAndReturn()
```


```
create()
```

The following example results in two INSERT statements:

```
INSERT
```


```
import { Prisma, PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ log: ["query"] }); async function main() { let users: Prisma.UserCreateInput[] = [ { email: "ariana@prisma.io", name: "Ari", profileViews: 20, coinflips: [true, false, false], role: "ADMIN", }, { email: "elsa@prisma.io", name: "Elsa", profileViews: 20, coinflips: [true, false, false], role: "ADMIN", }, ]; await Promise.all( users.map(async (user) => { await prisma.user.create({ data: user, }); }), ); } main() .then(async () => { await prisma.$disconnect(); }) .catch(async (e) => { console.error(e); await prisma.$disconnect(); process.exit(1); });
```


```
import { Prisma, PrismaClient } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const prisma = new PrismaClient({ log: ["query"] }); async function main() { let users: Prisma.UserCreateInput[] = [ { email: "ariana@prisma.io", name: "Ari", profileViews: 20, coinflips: [true, false, false], role: "ADMIN", }, { email: "elsa@prisma.io", name: "Elsa", profileViews: 20, coinflips: [true, false, false], role: "ADMIN", }, ]; await Promise.all( users.map(async (user) => { await prisma.user.create({ data: user, }); }), ); } main() .then(async () => { await prisma.$disconnect(); }) .catch(async (e) => { console.error(e); await prisma.$disconnect(); process.exit(1); });
```


This section covers the usage of the upsert() operation. To learn about using [nested upsert queries](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#upsert-1) within update(), reference the linked documentation.

```
upsert()
```


```
update()
```

upsert does the following:

```
upsert
```

- If an existing database record satisfies the where condition, it updates that record
- If no database record satisfies the where condition, it creates a new database record

```
where
```


```
where
```

#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-6)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-6)
- To perform arithmetic operations on update (add, subtract, multiply, divide), use [atomic updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#atomic-number-operations) to prevent race conditions.
- If two or more upsert operations happen at the same time and the record doesn't already exist, then a race condition might happen. As a result, one or more of the upsert operations might throw a unique key constraint error. Your application code can catch this error and retry the operation. [Learn more](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts).
- Prisma ORM hands over upsert queries to the database where possible. [Learn more](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upserts).
[atomic updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#atomic-number-operations)
[Learn more](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts)
[Learn more](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upserts)

#### [Unique key constraint errors on upserts](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts)
[Unique key constraint errors on upserts](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts)

##### [Problem](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#problem)
[Problem](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#problem)

### [upsert()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#upsert)

If multiple upsert operations happen at the same time and the record doesn't already exist, then one or more of the operations might return a [unique key constraint error](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/reference/error-reference#p2002).

##### [Cause](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#cause)
[Cause](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#cause)
When Prisma Client does an upsert, it first checks whether that record already exists in the database. To make this check, Prisma Client performs a read operation with the where clause from the upsert operation. This has two possible outcomes, as follows:

```
where
```

- If the record does not exist, then Prisma Client creates that record.
- If the record exists, then Prisma Client updates it.
When your application tries to perform two or more concurrent upsert operations, then a race condition might happen where two or more operations do not find the record and therefore try to create that record. In this situation, one of the operations successfully creates the new record but the other operations fail and return a unique key constraint error.

##### [Solution](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#solution)
[Solution](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#solution)
Handle the P2002 error in your application code. When it occurs, retry the upsert operation to update the row.

#### [Database upserts](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upserts)
[Database upserts](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upserts)
Where possible, Prisma Client hands over an upsert query to the database. This is called a database upsert.

```
upsert
```

Database upserts have the following advantages:
- They are faster than upserts handled by Prisma Client
- [Unique key constraint errors](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts) cannot happen
[Unique key constraint errors](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#unique-key-constraint-errors-on-upserts)
Prisma Client uses a database upsert automatically when [specific criteria](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-query-criteria) are met. When these criteria are not met, Prisma Client handles the upsert.

```
upsert
```

To use a database upsert, Prisma Client sends the SQL construction [INSERT ... ON CONFLICT SET .. WHERE](https://www.prisma.io/dataguide/postgresql/inserting-and-modifying-data/insert-on-conflict) to the database.

```
INSERT ... ON CONFLICT SET .. WHERE
```


##### [Database upsert prerequisites](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-prerequisites)
[Database upsert prerequisites](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-prerequisites)
Prisma Client uses database upserts with CockroachDB, PostgreSQL, or SQLite data sources.

##### [Database upsert query criteria](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-query-criteria)
[Database upsert query criteria](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-query-criteria)
Prisma Client uses a database upsert for an upsert query when the query meets the following criteria:

```
upsert
```

- There are no nested queries in the upsert's create and update [options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-7)
- The query does not include a selection that uses a [nested read](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#nested-reads)
- The query modifies only one model
- There is only one unique field in the upsert's where option
- The unique field in the where option and the unique field in the create option have the same value

```
upsert
```


```
create
```


```
update
```

[options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#options-7)
[nested read](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#nested-reads)

```
upsert
```


```
where
```


```
where
```


```
create
```

If your query does not meet these criteria, then Prisma Client handles the upsert itself.

##### [Database upsert examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-examples)
[Database upsert examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#database-upsert-examples)
The following examples use this schema:

```
model User { id Int @id profileViews Int userName String @unique email String @@unique([id, profileViews]) }
```


```
model User { id Int @id profileViews Int userName String @unique email String @@unique([id, profileViews]) }
```

The following upsert query meets all of the criteria, so Prisma Client uses a database upsert.

```
upsert
```

### [upsert()](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#upsert)

```
prisma.user.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```


```
prisma.user.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```

In this situation, Prisma uses the following SQL query:

```
INSERT INTO "public"."User" ("id","profileViews","userName","email") VALUES ($1,$2,$3,$4) ON CONFLICT ("userName") DO UPDATE SET "email" = $5 WHERE ("public"."User"."userName" = $6 AND 1=1) RETURNING "public"."User"."id", "public"."User"."profileViews", "public"."User"."userName", "public"."User"."email"
```


```
INSERT INTO "public"."User" ("id","profileViews","userName","email") VALUES ($1,$2,$3,$4) ON CONFLICT ("userName") DO UPDATE SET "email" = $5 WHERE ("public"."User"."userName" = $6 AND 1=1) RETURNING "public"."User"."id", "public"."User"."profileViews", "public"."User"."userName", "public"."User"."email"
```

The following query has multiple unique values in the where clause, so Prisma Client does not use a database upsert:

```
where
```


```
prisma.User.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", profileViews: 1, id: 1, }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```


```
prisma.User.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", profileViews: 1, id: 1, }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```

In the following query, the values for userName in the where and create options are different, so Prisma Client does not use a database upsert.

```
userName
```


```
where
```


```
create
```


```
prisma.User.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "AliceS", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```


```
prisma.User.upsert({ where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "AliceS", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```

In the following query, the selection on the title field in posts is a nested read, so Prisma Client does not use a database upsert.

```
title
```


```
posts
```


```
prisma.user.upsert({ select: { email: true, id: true, posts: { select: { title: true, }, }, }, where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });
```


```
prisma.user.upsert({ select: { email: true, id: true, posts: { select: { title: true, }, }, }, where: { userName: "Alice", }, create: { id: 1, profileViews: 1, userName: "Alice", email: "alice@prisma.io", }, update: { email: "updated@example.com", }, });

```
```
city

```
```
profileViews
```

```
200
```

```

```

### [relationLoadStrategy (Preview)](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#relationloadstrategy-preview)

[relationLoadStrategy (Preview)](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#relationloadstrategy-preview)

```
relationLoadStrategy
```

relationLoadStrategy specifies how a relation should be loaded from the database. It has two possible values:

```
relationLoadStrategy
```

- join (default): Uses a database-level LATERAL JOIN (PostgreSQL) or correlated subqueries (MySQL) and fetches all data with a single query to the database.
- query: Sends multiple queries to the database (one per table) and joins them on the application level.

```
join
```


```
LATERAL JOIN
```


```
query
```

Note: Once relationLoadStrategy moves from [Preview](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/more/releases#preview) into [General Availability](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/more/releases#generally-available-ga), join will universally become the default for all relation queries.

```
relationLoadStrategy
```


```
join
```

You can learn more about join strategies [here](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#relation-load-strategies-preview).
Because the relationLoadStrategy option is currently in Preview, you need to enable it via the relationJoins preview feature flag in your Prisma schema file:

```
relationLoadStrategy
```


```
relationJoins
```


```
generator client { provider = "prisma-client" output = "./generated" previewFeatures = ["relationJoins"] }
```


```
generator client { provider = "prisma-client" output = "./generated" previewFeatures = ["relationJoins"] }
```

After adding this flag, you need to run prisma generate again to re-generate Prisma Client. The relationJoins feature is currently available on PostgreSQL, CockroachDB and MySQL.

```
prisma generate
```


```
relationJoins
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-13)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-13)
- In most situations, the default join strategy will be more effective. Use query if you want to save resources on your database server or if you profiling shows that the application-level join is more performant.
- You can only specify the relationLoadStrategy on the top-level in your query. The top-level choice will affect all nested sub-queries.

```
join
```


```
query
```


```
relationLoadStrategy
```


#### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-21)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-21)

##### [Load the posts relation via a database-level JOIN when using include](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#load-the-posts-relation-via-a-database-level-join-when-using-include)
[Load the posts relation via a database-level JOIN when using include](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#load-the-posts-relation-via-a-database-level-join-when-using-include)

```
posts
```


```
include
```


```
const users = await prisma.user.findMany({ relationLoadStrategy: "join", include: { posts: true, }, });
```


```
const users = await prisma.user.findMany({ relationLoadStrategy: "join", include: { posts: true, }, });
```

### [where](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#where)

[where](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#where)

```
where
```

where defines one or more [filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#filter-conditions-and-operators), and can be used to filter on record properties (like a user's email address) or related record properties (like a user's top 10 most recent post titles).

```
where
```


#### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-22)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-22)

```
const results = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { email: { endsWith: "prisma.io", }, }, });
```


```
const results = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { email: { endsWith: "prisma.io", }, }, });
```


#### [Generated types for where](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#generated-types-for-where)
[Generated types for where](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#generated-types-for-where)

```
where
```

The following examples demonstrate how to use TypeScript's satisfies operator with where:

```
satisfies
```


```
where
```

- 
UserWhereInput
// UserWhereInput
const whereNameIs = { name: "Rich" } satisfies Prisma.UserWhereInput;

// It can be combined with conditional operators too
const whereNameIsWithAnd = {
  name: "Rich",
  AND: [
    {
      email: {
        contains: "rich@boop.com",
      },
    },
  ],
} satisfies Prisma.UserWhereInput;

- 
UserWhereUniqueInput This type works by exposing any unique fields on the model. A field assigned @id is considered unique,
as is one assigned @unique.
This type exposes all fields on the model. This means that when you filter for a single record based on a unique field, you can check additional non-unique and unique fields at the same time. [Learn more](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#filter-on-non-unique-fields-with-userwhereuniqueinput).
// UserWhereUniqueInput
const whereEmailIsUnique = { email: "rich@boop.com" } satisfies Prisma.UserWhereUniqueInput;

- 
PostScalarWhereInput
const whereScalarTitleIs = { title: "boop" } satisfies Prisma.PostScalarWhereInput;

- 
PostUpdateWithWhereUniqueWithoutAuthorInput - This type accepts a unique where field (an @id or another assigned @unique)
and updates any field on the Post model except the Author. The Author is the scalar field on the Post model.
const updatePostByIdWithoutAuthor = {
  where: { id: 1 },
  data: {
    content: "This is some updated content",
    published: true,
    title: "This is a new title",
  },
} satisfies Prisma.PostUpdateWithWhereUniqueWithoutAuthorInput;

- 
PostUpsertWithWhereUniqueWithoutAuthorInput - This type will update the Post records title field where the id matches, if it doesn't exist it will create it instead.
const updatePostTitleOrCreateIfNotExist = {
  where: { id: 1 },
  update: { title: "This is a new title" },
  create: {
    id: 1,
    title: "If the title doesn't exist, then create one with this text",
  },
} satisfies Prisma.PostUpsertWithWhereUniqueWithoutAuthorInput;

- 
PostUpdateManyWithWhereWithoutAuthorInput - This type will update all Post records where published is set to false.
const publishAllPosts = {
  where: { published: { equals: false } },
  data: { published: true },
} satisfies Prisma.PostUpdateManyWithWhereWithoutAuthorInput;

UserWhereInput

```

```

### [orderBy](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#orderby)

[orderBy](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#orderby)

```
orderBy
```

Sorts a list of records. See also: [Sorting](https://pris.ly/docs/v6/orm/prisma-client/queries/filtering-and-sorting)

#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-14)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-14)
- You can [order by relation fields](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-the-related-user-records-name) - for example, order posts by the author's name.
- In PostgreSQL you can [order by relevance](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-relevance-of-the-title). For details, see [Sort by relevance](https://pris.ly/docs/v6/orm/prisma-client/queries/filtering-and-sorting#sort-by-relevance-postgresql-and-mysql).
- You can [sort null records first or last](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-the-related-user-records-name-with-null-records-first). For details, see [Sort with nulls first or last](https://pris.ly/docs/v6/orm/prisma-client/queries/filtering-and-sorting#sort-with-null-records-first-or-last).
[order by relation fields](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-the-related-user-records-name)
[order by relevance](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-relevance-of-the-title)
[Sort by relevance](https://pris.ly/docs/v6/orm/prisma-client/queries/filtering-and-sorting#sort-by-relevance-postgresql-and-mysql)
[sort null records first or last](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#sort-post-by-the-related-user-records-name-with-null-records-first)

```
null
```

[Sort with nulls first or last](https://pris.ly/docs/v6/orm/prisma-client/queries/filtering-and-sorting#sort-with-null-records-first-or-last)


#### [Inputs for nulls argument](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#inputs-for-nulls-argument)

```
nulls
```

Note:
- This argument is optional.
- For use on optional [scalar](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#scalar-fields) fields only. If you try to sort by nulls on a required or [relation](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#relation-fields) field, Prisma Client throws a [P2009 error](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/reference/error-reference#p2009).
[scalar](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#scalar-fields)
[relation](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#relation-fields)
[P2009 error](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/reference/error-reference#p2009)

The order of sorting parameters matters - the following query sorts by role, then email. Note the difference in the results:

```
role
```


```
email
```


```
const users = await prisma.user.findMany({ select: { email: true, role: true, }, orderBy: [ { role: "desc", }, { email: "desc", }, ], });
```

## [nativeDistinct](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nativedistinct)
[nativeDistinct](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nativedistinct)

```
nativeDistinct
```

Enabling nativeDistinct in your Prisma schema pushes the distinct operation to the database layer (where supported). This can significantly improve performance. However, note that:

```
nativeDistinct
```


```
distinct
```

- Some databases may not fully support DISTINCT on certain field combinations.
- Behavior can differ among providers.
To enable nativeDistinct:

```
nativeDistinct
```


```
generator client { provider = "prisma-client" output = "./generated" previewFeatures = ["nativeDistinct"] }
```


```
generator client { provider = "prisma-client" output = "./generated" previewFeatures = ["nativeDistinct"] }
```

See [Preview Features](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/reference/preview-features/client-preview-features#preview-features-promoted-to-general-availability) for more details.

### [create](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#create-1)

[create](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#create-1)

```
create
```

A nested create query adds a new related record or set of records to a parent record. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries)

```
create
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-15)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-15)
- create is available as a nested query when you create() (prisma.user.create(...)) a new parent record or update() (prisma.user.update(...)) an existing parent record.
- You can use a nested create or a nested [createMany](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#createmany-1) to create multiple related records. If you require the [skipDuplicates query option](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-createmany-options) you should use createMany.

```
create
```


```
create()
```


```
prisma.user.create(...)
```


```
update()
```


```
prisma.user.update(...)
```

```
create
```

```
createMany
```

```
skipDuplicates
```

### [createMany](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#createmany-1)

[createMany](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#createmany-1)

```
createMany
```

A nested createMany query adds a new set of records to a parent record. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries)

```
createMany
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-16)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-16)
- createMany is available as a nested query when you create() (prisma.user.create(...)) a new parent record or update() (prisma.user.update(...)) an existing parent record.

Available in the context of a one-to-many relation — for example, you can prisma.user.create(...) a user and use a nested createMany to create multiple posts (posts have one user).
Not available in the context of a many-to-many relation — for example, you cannot prisma.post.create(...) a post and use a nested createMany to create categories (many posts have many categories).


- Available in the context of a one-to-many relation — for example, you can prisma.user.create(...) a user and use a nested createMany to create multiple posts (posts have one user).
- Not available in the context of a many-to-many relation — for example, you cannot prisma.post.create(...) a post and use a nested createMany to create categories (many posts have many categories).
- You cannot nest an additional create or createMany.
- Allows setting foreign keys directly — for example, setting the categoryId on a post.
- Nested createMany is supported by SQLite.
- You can use a nested create or a nested createMany to create multiple related records - [if you do not need the skipDuplicates query option, you should probably use create](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#create-a-single-record-and-multiple-related-records).

```
createMany
```


```
create()
```


```
prisma.user.create(...)
```


```
update()
```


```
prisma.user.update(...)
```

- Available in the context of a one-to-many relation — for example, you can prisma.user.create(...) a user and use a nested createMany to create multiple posts (posts have one user).
- Not available in the context of a many-to-many relation — for example, you cannot prisma.post.create(...) a post and use a nested createMany to create categories (many posts have many categories).

```
prisma.user.create(...)
```


```
createMany
```


```
prisma.post.create(...)
```


```
createMany
```


```
create
```


```
createMany
```


```
categoryId
```



```
create
```


```
createMany
```

[if you do not need the skipDuplicates query option, you should probably use create](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#create-a-single-record-and-multiple-related-records)

```
skipDuplicates
```


```
create
```


#### [Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-createmany-options)
[Options](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-createmany-options)

```

```


### [connect](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#connect)

[connect](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#connect)

```
connect
```

A nested connect query connects a record to an existing related record by specifying an ID or unique identifier. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries)

```
connect
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-17)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-17)
- 
connect is available as a nested query when you create a new parent record or update an existing parent record.

- 
If the related record does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:
The required connected records were not found. Expected 1 records to be connected, found 0.

- 
When using set and connect together, the order in which they are applied significantly impacts the result. If set is used before connect, the connected records will only reflect the final state established by the connect operation, as set clears all existing connections before connect establishes new ones. Conversely, if connect is applied before set, the set operation will override the connect action by clearing all connected records and replacing them with its own specified state.

connect is available as a nested query when you create a new parent record or update an existing parent record.

```
connect
```

If the related record does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:

```
The required connected records were not found. Expected 1 records to be connected, found 0.
```


```
The required connected records were not found. Expected 1 records to be connected, found 0.
```

When using set and connect together, the order in which they are applied significantly impacts the result. If set is used before connect, the connected records will only reflect the final state established by the connect operation, as set clears all existing connections before connect establishes new ones. Conversely, if connect is applied before set, the set operation will override the connect action by clearing all connected records and replacing them with its own specified state.

```
set
```


```
connect
```


```
set
```


```
connect
```


```
connect
```


```
set
```


```
connect
```


```
connect
```


```
set
```


```
set
```


```
connect
```

[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-28)

You can also set the foreign key directly:

```


```

However, you can't use both the direct approach and the connect approach in the same query. See [this issue comment](https://github.com/prisma/prisma/issues/4322#issuecomment-737976117) for details.

### [connectOrCreate](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#connectorcreate)

[connectOrCreate](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#connectorcreate)

```
connectOrCreate
```

connectOrCreate either connects a record to an existing related record by ID or unique identifier or creates a new related record if the record does not exist. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries)

```
connectOrCreate
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-18)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-18)
Multiple connectOrCreate queries that run as concurrent transactions can result in a race condition. Consider the following example, where two queries attempt to connectOrCreate a blog post tag named computing at the same time (tag names must be unique):

```
connectOrCreate
```


```
connectOrCreate
```


```
computing
```


```
const createPost = await prisma.post.create({ data: { title: "How to create a compiler", content: "...", author: { connect: { id: 9, }, }, tags: { connectOrCreate: { create: { name: "computing", }, where: { name: "computing", }, }, }, }, });
```


```
const createPost = await prisma.post.create({ data: { title: "How to create a compiler", content: "...", author: { connect: { id: 9, }, }, tags: { connectOrCreate: { create: { name: "computing", }, where: { name: "computing", }, }, }, }, });
```

If query A and query B overlap in the following way, query A results in an exception:

```
tagName
```


```
computing
```


```
tagName
```


```
computing
```


```
tagName
```


```
computing
```


```
tagName
```


```
computing
```

To work around this scenario, we recommend catching the unique violation exception (PrismaClientKnownRequestError, error P2002) and retrying failed queries.

```
PrismaClientKnownRequestError
```


```
P2002
```

### [disconnect](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#disconnect)
[disconnect](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#disconnect)

```
disconnect
```

A nested disconnect query breaks the connection between a parent record and a related record, but does not delete either record. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries)

```
disconnect
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-19)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-19)
- disconnect is only available if the relation is optional.
- If the relationship you are attempting to disconnect does not exist, the operation does nothing.

```
disconnect
```

### [update](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#update-1)

[update](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#update-1)

```
update
```

A nested update query updates one or more related records where the parent record's ID is n. See: [Working with relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#update-a-specific-related-record)

```
update
```


```
n
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-20)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-20)
- 
Nested update queries are only available in the context of a top-level update query (for example, prisma.user.update(...)).

- 
If the parent record does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")

- 
If the related record that you want to update does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")

Nested update queries are only available in the context of a top-level update query (for example, prisma.user.update(...)).

```
update
```


```
update
```


```
prisma.user.update(...)
```

If the parent record does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:

```
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")
```


```
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")
```

If the related record that you want to update does not exist, Prisma Client throws an exception:

```
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")
```


```
AssertionError("Expected a valid parent ID to be present for nested update to-one case.")
```

#### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-36)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-36)
Return all users where name equals "Eleanor"

## [Scalar list filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#scalar-list-filters)

[Scalar list filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#scalar-list-filters)
Scalar list filters allow you to filter by the contents of a list / array field.
Available for PostgreSQL, CockroachDB, and MongoDB.

### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-28)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-28)
- Scalar list / array filters [ignore NULL values](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-scalar-lists-arrays#null-values-in-arrays) . Using isEmpty or NOT does not return records with NULL value lists / arrays, and { equals: null } results in an error.
[ignore NULL values](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-scalar-lists-arrays#null-values-in-arrays)

```
NULL
```


```
isEmpty
```


```
NOT
```


```
NULL
```


```
{ equals: null }
```

  { height: 100, width: 200, url: "2.jpg" },
];

## [Composite type filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#composite-type-filters)

[Composite type filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#composite-type-filters)
Composite type filters allow you to filter the contents of [composite types](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/composite-types) (MongoDB only).

### [equals](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#equals-2)
[equals](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#equals-2)

```
equals
```

Use equals to filter results by matching a composite type or a list of composite types. Requires all required fields of the composite type to match.

```
equals
```


#### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-32)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-32)
When matching optional fields, you need to distinguish between undefined (missing) fields of the document, and fields that have been explicitly set to null:

```
null
```

- If you omit an optional field, it will match undefined fields, but not fields that have been set to null
- If you filter for null values of an optional field with equals: { ... exampleField: null ... }, then it will match only documents where the field has been set to null, and not undefined fields

```
null
```


```
null
```


```
equals: { ... exampleField: null ... }
```


```
null
```

The ordering of fields and lists matters when using equals:

```
equals
```

- For fields, { "a": "1", "b": "2" } and { "b": "2", "a": "1" } are not considered equal
- For lists, [ { "a": 1 }, { "a": 2 } ] and [ { "a": 2 }, { "a": 1 } ] are not considered equal

```
{ "a": "1", "b": "2" }
```


```
{ "b": "2", "a": "1" }
```


```
[ { "a": 1 }, { "a": 2 } ]
```


```
[ { "a": 2 }, { "a": 1 } ]
```


#### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-71)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-71)

##### [Find orders that exactly match the given shippingAddress](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#find-orders-that-exactly-match-the-given-shippingaddress)
[Find orders that exactly match the given shippingAddress](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#find-orders-that-exactly-match-the-given-shippingaddress)

```
shippingAddress
```


```
const orders = await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { shippingAddress: { equals: { street: "555 Candy Cane Lane", city: "Wonderland", zip: "52337", }, }, }, });
```


```
const orders = await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { shippingAddress: { equals: { street: "555 Candy Cane Lane", city: "Wonderland", zip: "52337", }, }, }, });
```


##### [Find products with photos that match all of a list of urls](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#find-products-with-photos-that-match-all-of-a-list-of-urls)
[Find products with photos that match all of a list of urls](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#find-products-with-photos-that-match-all-of-a-list-of-urls)

```

```


```
const product = prisma.product.findMany({ where: { equals: { photos: [{ url: "1.jpg" }, { url: "2.jpg" }], }, }, });
```



## [Atomic number operations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#atomic-number-operations)

[Atomic number operations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#atomic-number-operations)
Atomic operations on update is available for number field types (Float and Int). This feature allows you to update a field based on its current value (such as subtracting or dividing) without risking a race condition.

```
Float
```


```
Int
```

A race conditions occurs when two or more operations must be done in sequence in order to complete a task. In the following example, two clients try to increase the same field (postCount) by one:

```
postCount
```


```
21
```


```
21
```


```
22
```


```
22
```

The value should be 23, but the two clients did not read and write to the postCount field in sequence. Atomic operations on update combine read and write into a single operation, which prevents a race condition:

```
23
```


```
postCount
```


```
21
```


```
22
```


```
22
```


```
23
```

### [Operators](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#operators)
[Operators](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#operators)

```
increment
```


```
n
```


```
decrement
```


```
n
```


```
multiply
```


```
n
```


```
divide
```


```
n
```


```
set
```


```
{ myField : n }
```

### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-33)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-33)
- You can only perform one atomic update per field, per query.
- If a field is null, it will not be updated by increment, decrement, multiply, or divide.

```
null
```


```
increment
```


```
decrement
```


```
multiply
```


```
divide
```

### [Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-78)
[Examples](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#examples-78)

```
view
```

## [Json filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#json-filters)

[Json filters](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#json-filters)

```
Json
```

For use cases and advanced examples, see: [Working with Json fields](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-json-fields).

```
Json
```

Supported by [PostgreSQL](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/core-concepts/supported-databases/postgresql) and [MySQL](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/core-concepts/supported-databases/mysql) with different syntaxes for the path option. PostgreSQL does not support filtering on object key values in arrays.

```
path
```

The examples in this section assumes that the value of the pet field is:

```
pet
```


```
{ "favorites": { "catBreed": "Turkish van", "dogBreed": "Rottweiler", "sanctuaries": ["RSPCA", "Alley Cat Allies"], "treats": [ { "name": "Dreamies", "manufacturer": "Mars Inc" }, { "name": "Treatos", "manufacturer": "The Dog People" } ] }, "fostered": { "cats": ["Bob", "Alice", "Svetlana the Magnificent", "Queenie"] }, "owned": { "cats": ["Elliott"] } }
```


```
{ "favorites": { "catBreed": "Turkish van", "dogBreed": "Rottweiler", "sanctuaries": ["RSPCA", "Alley Cat Allies"], "treats": [ { "name": "Dreamies", "manufacturer": "Mars Inc" }, { "name": "Treatos", "manufacturer": "The Dog People" } ] }, "fostered": { "cats": ["Bob", "Alice", "Svetlana the Magnificent", "Queenie"] }, "owned": { "cats": ["Elliott"] } }
```

### [Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-34)
[Remarks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#remarks-34)
- The implementation of Json filtering [differs between database connectors](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-json-fields)
- Filtering is case sensitive in PostgreSQL and does not yet support mode

```
Json
```

[differs between database connectors](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-json-fields)

```
mode
```

### [path](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#path)
[path](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#path)

```
path
```

path represents the location of a specific key. The following query returns all users where the nested favorites > dogBreed key equals "Rottweiler".

```
path
```


```
favorites
```


```
dogBreed
```


```
"Rottweiler"
```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: ["favorites", "dogBreed"], equals: "Rottweiler", }, }, });
```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: ["favorites", "dogBreed"], equals: "Rottweiler", }, }, });
```

The following query returns all users where the nested owned > cats array contains "Elliott".

```
owned
```


```
cats
```


```
"Elliott"
```


```

```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: ["owned", "cats"], array_contains: ["Elliott"], }, }, });
```

Filtering by the key values of objects inside an array (below) is only supported by the MySQL connector.
The following query returns all users where the nested favorites > treats array contains an object where the name value is "Dreamies":

```
favorites
```


```
treats
```


```
name
```


```
"Dreamies"
```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: "$.favorites.treats[*].name", array_contains: "Dreamies", }, }, });
```



### [mode](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#mode-1)
[mode](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#mode-1)

```
mode
```

Specify whether the string filtering should be case sensitive (default) or case insensitive.
The following query returns all users where the nested favorites > catBreed key value contains "Van" or "van":

```
favorites
```


```
catBreed
```


```
"Van"
```


```
"van"
```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: ["favorites", "catBreed"], string_contains: "Van", mode: "insensitive", }, }, });
```


```
const getUsers = await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { pets: { path: ["favorites", "catBreed"], string_contains: "Van", mode: "insensitive", }, }, });
```

```
array_contains
```

```
sanctuaries
```

## [Utility types](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#utility-types)

[Utility types](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#utility-types)
Utility types are helper functions and types that live on the Prisma namespace. They are useful for keeping your application type safe.

```
Prisma
```

### [Type-checking with satisfies](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#type-checking-with-satisfies)

[Type-checking with satisfies](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#type-checking-with-satisfies)

```
satisfies
```

You can use TypeScript's satisfies operator to create re-usable query parameters based on your schema models while ensuring that the objects you create are type-compatible with the generated Prisma Client types. See also: [Type safety with Prisma Client](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/type-safety).

```
satisfies
```

Use the generated Prisma Client types with satisfies to get type checking and inference:

```
satisfies
```


```
const args = { ... } satisfies Prisma.GeneratedType;
```


```
const args = { ... } satisfies Prisma.GeneratedType;
```


#### [Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-3)
[Example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#example-3)
The following example shows how you can create type-checked input for the create operation that you can reuse within your app:

```
create
```


```
import { Prisma } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const createUserAndPostInput = ( name: string, email: string, postTitle: string, ) => ({ name, email, posts: { create: { title: postTitle, }, }, }) satisfies Prisma.UserCreateInput;
```


```
import { Prisma } from "../prisma/generated/client"; const createUserAndPostInput = ( name: string, email: string, postTitle: string, ) => ({ name, email, posts: { create: { title: postTitle, }, }, }) satisfies Prisma.UserCreateInput;
```

## [Compare columns in the same table](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#compare-columns-in-the-same-table)

[Compare columns in the same table](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#compare-columns-in-the-same-table)
You can compare columns in the same table directly, for non-unique filters.
In the following situations, you must [use raw queries to compare columns in the same table](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/more/troubleshooting/raw-sql-comparisons):
- If you want to use a unique filter, such as [findUnique](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findunique) or [findUniqueOrThrow](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow)
- If you want to compare a field with a [unique constraint](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#defining-a-unique-field)
- If you want to use one of the following operators to compare a [JSON field](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-json-fields) in MySQL or MariaDB with another field: [gt](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#gt), [gte](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#gte), [lt](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#lt), or [lte](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#lte). Note that you can use these operators to compare the JSON field with a scalar value. This limitation applies only if you try to compare a JSON field with another field.
[findUnique](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#findunique)

```
findUnique
```

[findUniqueOrThrow](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#finduniqueorthrow)

```
findUniqueOrThrow
```

[unique constraint](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/models#defining-a-unique-field)
[JSON field](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/special-fields-and-types/working-with-json-fields)
[gt](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#gt)

```
gt
```

[gte](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#gte)

```
gte
```

[lt](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#lt)

```
lt
```

[lte](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#lte)

```
lte
```

To compare columns in the same table, use the <model>.fields property. In the following example, the query returns all records where the value in the prisma.product.quantity field is less than or equal to the value in the prisma.product.warnQuantity field.

```
<model>.fields
```


```
prisma.product.quantity
```


```
prisma.product.warnQuantity
```


```
prisma.product.findMany({ where: { quantity: { lte: prisma.product.fields.warnQuantity } }, });
```


```
prisma.product.findMany({ where: { quantity: { lte: prisma.product.fields.warnQuantity } }, });
```

fields is a special property of every model. It contains the list of fields for that model.

```
fields
```

### [Considerations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#considerations)

[Considerations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#considerations)

#### [Fields must be of the same type](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#fields-must-be-of-the-same-type)
[Fields must be of the same type](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#fields-must-be-of-the-same-type)
You can only make comparisons on fields of the same type. For example, the following causes an error:

```
await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { id: { equals: prisma.order.fields.due }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // Type error: id is a string, while amountDue is an integer }, });
```


```
await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { id: { equals: prisma.order.fields.due }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // Type error: id is a string, while amountDue is an integer }, });
```


#### [Fields must be in the same model](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#fields-must-be-in-the-same-model)
[Fields must be in the same model](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#fields-must-be-in-the-same-model)
You can only make comparisons with the fields property on fields in the same model. The following example does not work:

```
fields
```


```
await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // Type error: name is a field on the User model, not Order }, });
```


```
await prisma.order.findMany({ where: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // Type error: name is a field on the User model, not Order }, });
```

However, you can compare fields in separate models with [standard queries](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#model-queries).

#### [In groupBy model queries, put your referenced fields in the by argument](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#in-groupby-model-queries-put-your-referenced-fields-in-the-by-argument)
[In groupBy model queries, put your referenced fields in the by argument](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#in-groupby-model-queries-put-your-referenced-fields-in-the-by-argument)

```
groupBy
```


```
by
```

If you use the [groupBy](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#groupby) model query with the having option, then you must put your referenced fields in the by argument.

```
having
```


```
by
```

The following example works:

```
prisma.user.groupBy({ by: ["id", "name"], having: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name } }, });
```


```
prisma.user.groupBy({ by: ["id", "name"], having: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name } }, });
```

The following example does not work, because name is not in the by argument:

```
name
```


```
by
```


```
prisma.user.groupBy({ by: ["id"], having: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name } }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // name is not in the 'by' argument });
```


```
prisma.user.groupBy({ by: ["id"], having: { id: { equals: prisma.user.fields.name } }, // ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^ // name is not in the 'by' argument });
```


#### [Search for fields in scalar lists](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#search-for-fields-in-scalar-lists)
[Search for fields in scalar lists](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#search-for-fields-in-scalar-lists)
If your data source supports scalar lists (for example [in](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#in) PostgreSQL), then you can search for all records where a specific field is in a list of fields. To do so, reference the scalar list with the in and [notIn](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#notin) filters. For example:

```
in
```


```
notIn
```


```
await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { // find all users where 'name' is in a list of tags name: { in: prisma.user.fields.tags }, }, });
```


```
await prisma.user.findMany({ where: { // find all users where 'name' is in a list of tags name: { in: prisma.user.fields.tags }, }, });
```

## [Filter on non-unique fields with UserWhereUniqueInput](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#filter-on-non-unique-fields-with-userwhereuniqueinput)

[Filter on non-unique fields with UserWhereUniqueInput](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#filter-on-non-unique-fields-with-userwhereuniqueinput)

```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```

The generated type UserWhereUniqueInput on [where](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#where) exposes all fields on the model, not just unique fields.

```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```


```
where
```

You must specify at least one unique field in your where statement [outside of boolean operators](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#boolean-operators-with-userwhereuniqueinput), and you can specify any number of additional unique and non-unique fields. You can use this to add filters to any operation that returns a single record. For example, you can use this feature for the following:

```
where
```

- [Optimistic concurrency control on updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#optimistic-concurrency-control-on-updates)
- [Permission checks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#permission-checks)
- [Soft deletes](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#soft-deletes)
- Filter on optional [one-to-one nested reads](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#nested-reads)
[Optimistic concurrency control on updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#optimistic-concurrency-control-on-updates)
[Permission checks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#permission-checks)
[Soft deletes](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#soft-deletes)
[one-to-one nested reads](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/relation-queries#nested-reads)

### [Optimistic concurrency control on updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#optimistic-concurrency-control-on-updates)
[Optimistic concurrency control on updates](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#optimistic-concurrency-control-on-updates)
You can filter on non-unique fields to perform [optimistic concurrency control](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#optimistic-concurrency-control) on update operations.

```
update
```

To perform optimistic concurrency control, use a version field to check whether the data in a record or related record has changed while your code executes.

```
version
```

In the following example, updateOne and updateTwo first read the same record and then attempt to update it. The database only executes these updates if the value in version is the same as the value when it did the initial read. When the database executes the first of these updates (which might be updateOne or updateTwo, depending on timing), it increments the value in version. This means that the database does not execute the second update because the value in version has changed.

```
updateOne
```


```
updateTwo
```


```
version
```


```
updateOne
```


```
updateTwo
```


```
version
```


```
version
```


```
model User { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) email String @unique city String version Int }
```


```
model User { id Int @id @default(autoincrement()) email String @unique city String version Int }
```


```
function updateOne() { const user = await prisma.user.findUnique({ id: 1 }); await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: user.id, version: user.version }, data: { city: "Berlin", version: { increment: 1 } }, }); } function updateTwo() { const user = await prisma.user.findUnique({ id: 1 }); await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: user.id, version: user.version }, data: { city: "New York", version: { increment: 1 } }, }); } function main() { await Promise.allSettled([updateOne(), updateTwo()]); }
```


```
function updateOne() { const user = await prisma.user.findUnique({ id: 1 }); await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: user.id, version: user.version }, data: { city: "Berlin", version: { increment: 1 } }, }); } function updateTwo() { const user = await prisma.user.findUnique({ id: 1 }); await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: user.id, version: user.version }, data: { city: "New York", version: { increment: 1 } }, }); } function main() { await Promise.allSettled([updateOne(), updateTwo()]); }
```

### [Permission checks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#permission-checks)
[Permission checks](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#permission-checks)
You can filter on non-unique fields to check permissions during an update.
In the following example, a user wants to update a post title. The where statement checks the value in authorId to confirm that the user is the author of the post. The application only updates the post title if the user is the post author.

```
where
```


```
authorId
```


```
await prisma.post.update({ where: { id: 1, authorId: 1 }, data: { title: "Updated post title" }, });
```


```
await prisma.post.update({ where: { id: 1, authorId: 1 }, data: { title: "Updated post title" }, });
```

### [Soft deletes](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#soft-deletes)
[Soft deletes](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#soft-deletes)
You can filter on non-unique fields to handle soft deletes.
In the following example, we do not want to return a post if it is soft-deleted. The operation only returns the post if the value in isDeleted is false.

```
isDeleted
```


```
false
```


```
prisma.Post.findUnique({ where: { id: postId, isDeleted: false } });
```


```
prisma.Post.findUnique({ where: { id: postId, isDeleted: false } });
```

### [UserWhereUniqueInput considerations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#userwhereuniqueinput-considerations)

[UserWhereUniqueInput considerations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#userwhereuniqueinput-considerations)

```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```


#### [Boolean operators with UserWhereUniqueInput](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#boolean-operators-with-userwhereuniqueinput)
[Boolean operators with UserWhereUniqueInput](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#boolean-operators-with-userwhereuniqueinput)

```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```

With UserWhereUniqueInput, you must specify at least one unique field outside of the boolean operators AND, OR, NOT. You can still use these boolean operators in conjunction with any other unique fields or non-unique fields in your filter.

```
UserWhereUniqueInput
```


```
AND
```


```
OR
```


```
NOT
```

In the following example, we test id, a unique field, in conjunction with email. This is valid.

```
id
```


```
email
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1, OR: [{ email: "bob@prisma.io" }, { email: "alice@prisma.io" }] }, // ^^^ Valid: the expression specifies a unique field (`id`) outside of any boolean operators data: { ... } }) // SQL equivalent: // WHERE id = 1 AND (email = "bob@prisma.io" OR email = "alice@prisma.io")
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1, OR: [{ email: "bob@prisma.io" }, { email: "alice@prisma.io" }] }, // ^^^ Valid: the expression specifies a unique field (`id`) outside of any boolean operators data: { ... } }) // SQL equivalent: // WHERE id = 1 AND (email = "bob@prisma.io" OR email = "alice@prisma.io")
```

The following example is not valid, because there is no unique field outside of any boolean operators:

```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { OR: [{ email: "bob@prisma.io" }, { email: "alice@prisma.io" }] }, // ^^^ Invalid: the expressions does not contain a unique field outside of boolean operators data: { ... } })
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { OR: [{ email: "bob@prisma.io" }, { email: "alice@prisma.io" }] }, // ^^^ Invalid: the expressions does not contain a unique field outside of boolean operators data: { ... } })
```


#### [One-to-one relations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#one-to-one-relations)
[One-to-one relations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#one-to-one-relations)
You can filter on non-unique fields in the following operations on [one-to-one relations](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-schema/data-model/relations/one-to-one-relations):
- Nested update
- Nested upsert
- Nested disconnect
- Nested delete
Prisma Client automatically uses a unique filter to select the appropriate related record. As a result, you do not need to specify a unique filter in your where statement with a WhereUniqueInput [generated type](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#generated-types-for-where). Instead, the where statement has a WhereInput generated type. You can use this to filter without the restrictions of WhereUniqueInput.

```
where
```


```
WhereUniqueInput
```


```
where
```


```
WhereInput
```


```
WhereUniqueInput
```


##### [Nested update example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-update-example)
[Nested update example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-update-example)

```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { update: { where: { /* WhereInput */ }, data: { field: "updated" } } } } })
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { update: { where: { /* WhereInput */ }, data: { field: "updated" } } } } })
```


##### [Nested upsert example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-upsert-example)
[Nested upsert example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-upsert-example)

```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { upsert: { where: { /* WhereInput */ }, create: { /* CreateInput */ }, update: { /* UpdateInput */ }, } } } })
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { upsert: { where: { /* WhereInput */ }, create: { /* CreateInput */ }, update: { /* UpdateInput */ }, } } } })
```


##### [Nested disconnect example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-disconnect-example)
[Nested disconnect example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-disconnect-example)

```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { disconnect: { /* WhereInput */ } } } })
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { disconnect: { /* WhereInput */ } } } })
```

### [UserWhereUniqueInput considerations](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#userwhereuniqueinput-considerations)

##### [Nested delete example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-delete-example)
[Nested delete example](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#nested-delete-example)

```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { delete: { /* WhereInput */ } } } })
```


```
await prisma.user.update({ where: { id: 1 }, data: { to_one: { delete: { /* WhereInput */ } } } })
```

## [PrismaPromise behavior](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#prismapromise-behavior)

[PrismaPromise behavior](https://pris.ly/d/client-constructor#prismapromise-behavior)

```
PrismaPromise
```

All Prisma Client queries return an instance of Prisma[Promise](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Promise). This is a ["thenable"](https://masteringjs.io/tutorials/fundamentals/thenable), meaning a PrismaPromise only executes when you call await or .then() or .catch(). This behavior is different from a regular JavaScript Promise, which starts executing immediately.

```
PrismaPromise
```


```
PrismaPromise
```


```
await
```


```
.then()
```


```
.catch()
```


```
Promise
```

For example:

```
const findPostOperation = prisma.post.findMany({}); // Query not yet executed findPostOperation.then(); // Prisma Client now executes the query // or await findPostOperation; // Prisma Client now executes the query
```


```
const findPostOperation = prisma.post.findMany({}); // Query not yet executed findPostOperation.then(); // Prisma Client now executes the query // or await findPostOperation; // Prisma Client now executes the query
```

When using the [$transaction API](https://pris.ly/docs/orm/prisma-client/queries/transactions#the-transaction-api), this behavior makes it possible for Prisma Client to pass all the queries on to the query engine as a single transaction.

```
$transaction
```
